### Question 2: Can you differentiate a cross-listed course and elective applied course in the case of a double major?  
### Answer: 

In the context provided, a cross-listed course refers to a course that is shared between two majors or a major and a minor, and it can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements up to a limit of 8 credits (two courses) per pair of majors or major-minor combination. An elective applied course, on the other hand, is a course from another major that emphasizes the applications of mathematics and must be taken for at least 2 courses, with at least one at the 200-level. Importantly, a student may not double count a course for two different requirements; for example, Operations Research can only count for either 1 Advanced or an elective applied course requirement, but not both. Therefore, while cross-listed courses can be shared between majors or minors to fulfill requirements, elective applied courses are specific to the application of mathematics and have their own distinct requirements and limitations. They cannot be used interchangeably with cross-listed courses for fulfilling different requirements.

and a minor) share cross- listed or tagged1 courses, up to 8 credits (two courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements. This limit is per each pair of majors (or major and minor) and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim. For example, a student can major in both A and B and minor in C with a total of 6 double-counted courses: two in A and B, two in B and C, and two in A and C. This rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed or tagged. For instance, if major A requires certain courses from major B for out-of-area foundation, exploration, or applications of the major, and these courses are not cross-listed between A and B, they do not count toward the 8-credit limit. 1 In interdisciplinary minors, the requirements mainly consist of courses from other majors. These courses are usually not cross-listed with the minors and are referred to as 'tagged' by these minors. 13.4  Experiential Learning Requirements Experiential Learning can

For example, an exploratory course can also be counted as a major course for the corresponding major. However, the number of double-counted credits is often limited (e.g., see subsections 13.2 and 13.3). Additionally, any particular course can only be used to satisfy at most two requirements. For instance, if course X is cross-listed between major A and major B and tagged by minor C, then X can be used to fulfill the requirements of major A and major B, or major A and minor C, or major B and minor C. Triple counting is not allowed. 13.9  Maximal Length of Study Fulbright follows MOET regulations, which state that the maximum time to complete the program cannot exceed double the standard

### Question 3: I would like to ask for the capstone withdrawal policy. What will be the impact when I choose to drop the capstone before the Fall 2025 term starts? Will there be any penalties associated with withdrawing, such as a 'W' notation on my transcript?  
### Answer: 

According to the provided context, for the Fall 2025 term, if you withdraw from a course during the first withdrawal period (after 4:00 PM Friday, Week 2 to 4:00 PM Friday, Week 4), there will be no consequences in your academic record. However, if you withdraw from a course during the second withdrawal period (after 4:00 PM Friday, Week 4 to 4:00 PM Friday, Week 8), a "W" grade will be recorded on your transcript, but this grade does not affect your GPA.

Since the Capstone course is typically taken during the final term of study, it falls within the second withdrawal period. Therefore, if you choose to drop the Capstone before the Fall 2025 term starts, you will receive a "W" notation on your transcript, but this will not impact your GPA. 

Please note that you should still consult with your Academic/Major Advisor before withdrawing from the course to ensure you understand all implications and requirements specific to your program. Additionally, maintaining full-time enrollment status by registering for a minimum of 12 credits per term is important. If your withdrawal results in fewer than 12 academic credits, you may lose your full-time enrollment status, which could have financial aid implications. Tuition credit will be considered in cases of approved exceptional circumstances, but no reduction in tuition is granted for students whose course withdrawal results in fewer than 12 academic credits. 

In summary, there will be no penalties associated with withdrawing from the Capstone course before the Fall 2025 term starts, but a "W" notation will appear on your transcript. Ensure you follow the proper procedures and consult with your advisor to manage your academic and financial aid status appropriately.

### Question 4: Questions related to course history, in which one course can have multiple IDs? Like Advanced Deep Learning course. How would it be handled among different cohorts?  
### Answer: 

When a course like Advanced Deep Learning has multiple IDs and is offered to different cohorts, it typically means that the course content or structure may vary slightly between each offering. This could be due to updates in the curriculum, changes in instructors, or adjustments based on feedback from previous cohorts.

To handle this among different cohorts, institutions often maintain detailed records of each course iteration, including any changes made during the course of its offerings. This ensures that students in different cohorts receive consistent educational experiences despite the multiple IDs. Additionally, instructors might provide supplementary materials or clarify any discrepancies between iterations to help students understand how the course has evolved over time. In some cases, there might also be a standardized syllabus that outlines the core topics covered in the course, ensuring a common foundation for all cohorts.

### Question 5: I have taken Microeconomic Analysis and Macroeconomic Analysis in Fall 2023. Am I eligible to take Financial Economics in Spring 2024?  
### Answer: 

Yes, you are eligible to take Financial Economics in Spring 2024. According to the provided information, Advanced level courses in Economics can be taken after completing at least one of Microeconomic and Macroeconomic Analysis and Econometrics. Since you have already completed Microeconomic Analysis and Macroeconomic Analysis, you meet the prerequisite requirement to take Financial Economics in Spring 2024. However, please note that you might also need to ensure you meet any other prerequisites or requirements specific to the Financial Economics course itself.

Courses: Principles of Economics 1 and 2 (100-level) These two courses introduce microeconomics and macroeconomics, providing an overview of economic theories and analytical techniques applied to current issues. By studying both microeconomics (the analysis of choices made by people, firms, and governments) and macroeconomics (the analysis of the economy as a whole) students will develop their economic intuition as they better understand the functioning of the world. Methodology Courses: Economic Methods (100-level) This course introduces basic concepts and methods of statistical analysis and fundamental rules of mathematics used in economic analysis. Students will be exposed to a wide range of economic problems and the methods to solve them. By completing this course, students will be qualified to take upper-level courses in the Economics major. ### Question 6: If I have waived the course Computer Science I, but I want to declare Computer Science major, do I have to take Computer Science I?  
### Answer: 

No, you do not have to take Computer Science I if you have waived it. However, you still need to meet the prerequisites and complete the required courses for the major, including CS 101: Introduction to Programming, as stated in the major requirements. Waiving a course does not exempt you from fulfilling the major's course requirements.

### Question 7: If I have taken the following courses: Mathematical Statistics, Abstract Algebra, Linear Algebra, Multivariable Calculus, Calculus, Differential Equation, Stochastic Calculus, Statistical Learning, Discrete Mathematics, Probability, am I eligible to declare a minor in Applied Mathematics? What about majoring in Applied Mathematics?  
### Answer: 

Based on the information provided, you have taken several courses that align with the requirements for both a minor and a major in Applied Mathematics. Here's a breakdown:

### Minor in Applied Mathematics:
- **Foundation Courses**: You have completed Linear Algebra, Multivariable Calculus, and Introduction to Statistics (Mathematical Statistics).
- **Intermediate Courses**: You have completed Differential Equations, Discrete Mathematics, Probability, and Stochastic Calculus.
- **Advanced Courses**: You have completed Advanced Statistics (Mathematical Statistics), Statistical Learning, and Stochastic Calculus.

You meet the minimum requirement of 2 advanced courses and have covered most of the intermediate courses. However, you are missing some courses that are typically required for a minor, such as Numerical Analysis or another applied course. Therefore, you might be eligible for a minor in Applied Mathematics, but it depends on the specific institution's requirements. It is advisable to consult with an academic advisor to confirm eligibility.

### Major in Applied Mathematics:
To major in Applied Mathematics, you need to meet the following criteria:
- **Foundation Courses**: Linear Algebra, Multivariable Calculus, and Introduction to Statistics.
- **Intermediate Courses**: At least 2 intermediate courses (you have completed 6).
- **Advanced Courses**: At least 2 advanced courses (you have completed 4).

While you have met the majority of the requirements, you are still missing some courses. Specifically, you need to complete additional advanced courses and possibly an applied course. Again, consulting with an academic advisor is crucial to ensure you meet all the requirements for a major in Applied Mathematics.

In summary, you are likely eligible for a minor in Applied Mathematics, but you may need to complete additional courses to major in Applied Mathematics. Consulting with an academic advisor is recommended for confirmation.

### Question 9: Is it possible that I write a book as my History Capstone?  
### Answer: 

It is not explicitly mentioned in the provided context whether writing a book is a feasible option for the History Capstone project. The suggested alternative formats include a short documentary film, a podcast, a historical exhibition, or an interactive digital narrative. While these are the recommended alternatives, there is no explicit prohibition against writing a book. However, it would be advisable to consult with a potential advisor to discuss the feasibility and alignment of a book project with the Capstone requirements and learning outcomes. Writing a book might not align well with the expectation to 'work up' sources that do not figure extensively in existing scholarship. Therefore, while theoretically possible, it would require careful planning and discussion with an advisor.

Project Format There is no specific format requirement for the History Capstone project. Most students choose to write a traditional thesis (as of Fall 2024, all the History Capstone projects have adopted this format), but students are free to adopt other formats as well. Suggested alternative formats may include: ● a short documentary film, ● a podcast, ● a historical exhibition, or ● an interactive digital narrative. Students who expect to apply to postgraduate schools or enter writing-intensive careers after graduation may benefit most from the experience of authoring a written thesis based on archival materials or other primary sources (including oral history interviews), which they can furnish as a writing sample or use as the basis for a graduate thesis. The primary objective of the History Major Capstone is for students to produce a body of original historical research based on primary source evidence. The project generally takes the form of an undergraduate thesis; however students may design a non-traditional project with a substantial written component (e.g., a documentary, a museum exhibit, a digital database, an oral history archive, etc.). Students will design their Capstone project in close consultation with history faculty and receive scaffolded peer-review in the research design seminar. Capstone projects should reflect student specialization in at least one geographical, temporal, or thematic historical field and are encouraged to apply historical perspectives to problems in other disciplines. Capstone projects are eligible to be evaluated for honors. Requirements for Declaring the History Major and Minor In order to formally declare the History Major, students

[Source: History Capstone Handbook - 2025-26.pdf, Page: 9]
The Capstone project is a year-long undertaking with less structure than a traditional course. It is certainly not the easiest way to complete your degree, and it may not be the most logical option for you, depending on your interests and your post-graduation plans. You should not consider it to be the default pathway to finishing your degree. One of the best reasons to undertake a Capstone project is if you enjoy doing historical research (which you will have sampled in Hands-On History and the research seminars you have completed) and want an opportunity to carry out a long-term research project. For such students, the Capstone year provides time and guidance that is unparalleled by any course or other opportunity at the undergraduate level. However, if you wish to graduate with distinction—an honorable goal— but you don’t particularly enjoy doing independent research, you may want to skip the Capstone and focus on GPA honors instead! ### Question 11: I have a question if I take a gap year, will my financial aid be canceled? If yes, can I still re-apply for the financial aid program when I get back to school?  
### Answer: 

Based on the provided context, there is no explicit mention of whether financial aid would be canceled if you take a gap year. However, it is mentioned that you may lose eligibility for scholarships while on a leave of absence. 

To answer your specific questions:
1. Whether your financial aid would be canceled depends on the specific terms and conditions of your financial aid package and the policies of Fulbright University. Generally, taking a gap year might affect your eligibility for certain types of financial aid, but it doesn't necessarily mean it will be completely canceled.

2. You can typically re-apply for financial aid when you return to school, but you should contact the financial aid office at Fulbright University to confirm their specific policies regarding re-applying for financial aid after a gap year. They will be able to provide you with accurate and detailed information about your situation. 

It's important to meet with your Academic Advisor and the financial aid office to discuss your plans and ensure you understand all the implications of taking a gap year on your academic and financial standing. They can also help you develop a plan to successfully return to Fulbright to complete your degree.

### Question 13: If I major in Economics, is it sufficient that I take Scholar Development to fulfill Experiential Learning requirements?  
### Answer: 

No, taking Scholar Development alone is not sufficient to fulfill the Experiential Learning requirements for an Economics major. According to the provided information, students must complete at least 4 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the Experiential Learning Program (ELP) as a graduation requirement. Scholar Development may count toward elective or major requirements upon advisor approval, but it is not specifically mentioned as fulfilling the Experiential Learning requirements for Economics majors. Therefore, additional coursework or experiences need to be completed to meet this requirement.

### Question 14: Is it sufficient for me to complete 4 credits in EL if I major in Engineering?  
### Answer: 

Yes, it is sufficient to complete 4 credits in EL (Experiential Learning) if you major in Engineering. Specifically, the requirement states that students must complete "at least 01 Scholar Development (4 credits)." This means completing exactly 4 credits in Scholar Development, which falls under the Experiential Learning category, satisfies this requirement. The Scholar Development(s) must also be approved by the Chair of Engineering. Therefore, fulfilling this condition will meet the Experiential Learning requirement for your Engineering major.

### Question 15: Can I take all four engineering foundation courses and only two intermediate engineering courses?  
### Answer: 

No, you cannot take all four engineering foundation courses and only two intermediate engineering courses. According to the provided information, you need to take at least 3 courses at the 300-level or Advanced level (12 credits) out of the 9 Engineering major courses (36 credits). Therefore, taking only two intermediate engineering courses would not meet this requirement. You would need to take at least three advanced level courses to fulfill the degree requirements.

(AI) is a research ﬁeld that studies how to realize the intelligent human behaviors on a computer. The ultimate goal of AI is to make a computer that can learn, plan, and solve problems autonomously. In this course, student will learn the foundational principles and practice implementing some of these applications including representation, problem solving, and learning methods of artiﬁcial intelligence. ### Question 17: Does completing both Microeconomics and Macroeconomics satisfy the core theory requirement, or is an additional course needed?  
### Answer: 

Completing both Microeconomics and Macroeconomics satisfies the core theory requirement for the Economics major. No additional course is needed beyond these two courses.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Major Descriptions and Flowcharts_OfficialVersion.pdf, Page: 31]
Courses: Principles of Economics 1 and 2 (100-level) These two courses introduce microeconomics and macroeconomics, providing an overview of economic theories and analytical techniques applied to current issues. By studying both microeconomics (the analysis of choices made by people, firms, and governments) and macroeconomics (the analysis of the economy as a whole) students will develop their economic intuition as they better understand the functioning of the world. Methodology Courses: Economic Methods (100-level) This course introduces basic concepts and methods of statistical analysis and fundamental rules of mathematics used in economic analysis. Students will be exposed to a wide range of economic problems and the methods to solve them. By completing this course, students will be qualified to take upper-level courses in the Economics major. Prerequisites: None The Programming for Data Science and Visualization course aims at providing students with a set of skills to analyze the nature of data across diﬀerent domains. The course demonstrates data visualization by understanding, questioning, and problematizing how data are generated, analyzed, and used. The students will be able to apply concepts and skills to visualize data, interpret the ﬁndings, and examine the impacts of data-driven decision. The course will also get the students familiar with Python programming language and its libraries to analyze, visualize and discover data insight leading to a proper data-driven decision-making process. Prerequisites: None (CS104 is recommended) This course aims to equip students with the skills necessary to solve computational problems using a high-level programming language. Students will develop their abilities to use (i) fundamental programming constructs such as branching statements, loops, functions, and recursion and (ii) abstract data types such as lists and maps. Students will also be exposed to basic concepts of object-oriented programming. CS103: Programming for Data Science and Visualization Prerequisites: None The Programming for Data Science and Visualization course aims at providing students with a set of skills to analyze the nature of data across diﬀerent domains. The course demonstrates data visualization by understanding, questioning, and problematizing how data are generated, analyzed, and used. The students will be able to apply concepts and skills to visualize data, interpret the ﬁndings, and examine the impacts of data-driven decision. The course will also get the students familiar

### Question 19: Given I took Discrete Mathematics in Spring 2022 and earned B, then the same course in Spring 2024 and earned C-, which grades will be kept?  
### Answer: 

The grade that will be kept is the higher grade, which is B in this case. The lower grade, C-, will be overwritten by the notation "RP", meaning "repeated", and will remain on the transcript.

### Question 20: Can I register 300-level math courses as exploratory courses E4?  
### Answer: 

No, you cannot register 300-level math courses as exploratory courses E4. The context specifies that exploratory courses for E4-Mathematics and Computing are limited to 100-level or 200-level courses. Advanced courses like those at the 300 level are meant for shaping a study path into applied fields and do not count towards the exploratory requirements.

### Question 21: Can I register for more than 20 credits in a semester?  
### Answer: 

No, you cannot register for more than 20 credits in a semester according to the given context. The context specifies that students are required to register for no more than 20 credit hours per term to make standard progress toward completing the degree. To register for more than 20 credit hours, you would need to submit the Maximum Course Load Request form, which requires approval from your Academic Advisor and the Office of the Registrar.

Students pursuing a double major must complete all requirements for each major. If two majors (or two minors, or a major and a minor) share cross- listed or tagged1 courses, up to 8 credits (two courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements. This limit is per each pair of majors (or major and minor) and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim. For example, a student can major in both A and B and minor in C with a total of 6 double-counted courses: two in A and B, two in B and C, and two in A and C. This rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed or

All students for whom English is not their first language must take an English Assessment Test required by NECHE Accreditation. 13.8  Double Counting In satisfying degree requirements, some courses can be double-counted. For example, an exploratory course can also be counted as a major course for the corresponding major. However, the number of double-counted credits is often limited (e.g., see subsections 13.2 and 13.3). Additionally, any particular course can only be used to satisfy at most two requirements. For instance, if course X is cross-listed between major A and major B and tagged by minor C, then X can be used to fulfill the requirements of major A and major B, or major A and minor C, or major B and minor C. Triple counting is not allowed. 13.9  Maximal Length of Study Fulbright follows MOET regulations, which state that the maximum time to complete the program cannot exceed double the standard

### Question 22: What is the maximum number of times I can retake a course to improve my grade, and how does it affect my transcript?  
### Answer: 

According to the policy, you can retake the same course up to three times. However, you cannot retake the same course for the third time unless you failed the second time or if a specific grade is needed to meet the major requirements.

The lower grade will be overwritten by the notation "RP", meaning "repeated", and remain on the transcript. A higher grade will be kept and used in the GPA calculation. The credits of the repeated course are counted toward the total attempted credits. Therefore, the maximum number of times you can retake a course is three, but you must have a valid reason for the third attempt, such as failing the second time or needing a specific grade for your major.

### Question 23: For a student doing the literature capstone, if a student includes charts or tables, do they count toward the word limit?  
### Answer: 

Charts or tables do not count toward the word limit. The provided guidelines specify that the bibliography and images with captions are excluded from the word count. Therefore, any additional charts or tables would also be excluded from the word limit calculation.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Integrated Sciences_Capstone Handbook_14Jan2025.pdf, Page: 13]
2. Capstones by Thesis guidelines: 2.1. Word count regulations The written thesis is documentation of the capstone project, in the form of a research paper. There is no word count limit, but the thesis is usually 25-40 pages on A4 size. This page count includes full bibliography and images with captions. 2.2. Style and formatting The thesis should be typed with font size 12, suggested fonts are Calibri or Arial. The following parts should be included in order: • Title page • Committee signature page • Copyright page (do NOT number or add anything to this page, only change the template* to your name) • Acknowledgement page • Abstract • Table of contents • Introduction • Methods • Results • Discussion • Conclusions • References *Templates for the first 3 pages can be found on the Capstone II Canvas page. Following these general formatting guidelines, the details of the thesis and presentation should be worked out between the student and advisors. 2.3. ### Question 24: If I failed Capstone I in the Fall 2024, can I redo it in Spring 2025?  
### Answer: 

If you failed Capstone I in the Fall 2024, you cannot simply redo it in Spring 2025. Typically, you would need to plan your Independent Study (IS) courses to fulfill the major requirements since you did not pass Capstone I. You would need to discuss with your advisors and potentially adjust your project idea with them. Once you have addressed the issues that led to your failure, you might be given another chance to attempt Capstone I, but this would depend on the policies of your institution and the decisions of your advisors. It's important to act promptly and follow the guidelines provided by your academic institution.

If the students do not pass Capstone I, they should promptly plan their IS courses to fulfill the major requirements. 1.6. Capstone II In Capstone II you will focus mostly on conducting experiments, collecting data, doing analysis, and intepreting results. After getting results from each experiment, you should interpret how the results contribute to testing the hypotheses and answering the reseach question. Often the results of experiments would lead to futher testing, you should formulate your steps accordingly in consultation with your advisors. You will summarize the results of your project, from background investigation to final conclusions in a written thesis. In addition to this written submission , at the end of Capstone II, you will

[Source: History Capstone Handbook - 2025-26.pdf, Page: 9]
seminars you have completed) and want an opportunity to carry out a long-term research project. For such students, the Capstone year provides time and guidance that is unparalleled by any course or other opportunity at the undergraduate level. However, if you wish to graduate with distinction—an honorable goal— but you don’t particularly enjoy doing independent research, you may want to skip the Capstone and focus on GPA honors instead! Normally, the Capstone sequence begins in the Fall with Capstone I and ends in the Spring with Capstone II. It culminates with a formal defense and a final evaluation by two readers. Students work with a primary advisor and, to a lesser extent, a secondary advisor. The format and length of projects is flexible, within certain limits. This handbook explains each aspect of the Capstone experience so that you can plan ahead and know what to expect. 1.2. History Capstone Learning Outcomes Students who successfully complete a Capstone project will be able to: 1. Demonstrate

[Source: Integrated Sciences_Capstone Handbook_14Jan2025.pdf, Page: 12]
year, Fall semester Capstone I Varied, based on requirements from advisor(s). 4th year, Spring semester Capstone II Presentation and written thesis Table 2. Typical timeline of doing capstone projects in a 4-year study journey. It is important to manage the workload. A research project in the natural sciences takes a lot of time and effort and does not always produce the expected results. This frequently leads to reruns of experiments, longer processing time, and other setbacks. It is highly recommended that students complete as many of their graduate requirements prior to doing the capstone as possible and have good time management while doing the capstone. 1.1. Roles of the capstone in the Integrated Sciences curriculum The Integrated Sciences (IS) major is a single, comprehensive program comprising of different branches of natural science. Research is an important part of IS curriculum and the capstone is where students can bring together their skills and knowledge to execute a research project from

[Source: Integrated Sciences_Capstone Handbook_14Jan2025.pdf, Page: 12]
a primary advisor and in some cases, there is also a secondary advisor. Students then proceed to Capstone I, followed by Capstone II in the following semester if and only if they pass Capstone I. At the end of Capstone II, students will have an oral defense and submit their written thesis for grading. The general process is illustrated in table 2, assuming a normal 4-year journey. More details are included in the following sections. ### Question 25: If I do Literature capstone in Decolonial studies, can it be approved?  
### Answer: 

Based on the information provided, a capstone project in Decolonial studies could potentially be approved if there is faculty expertise in that field. The context states that projects for which there is no faculty expertise may not be approved. If they do, your project should be eligible for approval. If not, the project may not be approved. It's recommended to consult with prospective advisors early in your junior year to determine the suitability and feasibility of your proposed project.

1. General Information: The Literature Capstone is a culmination of a student’s curriculum through an individual project involving independent research. Through support from existing faculty, students propose, undertake, and write up a research or creative writing project over the course of two consecutive semesters, labelled as Capstone I and Capstone II. Students are encouraged to conduct primary and secondary research, even for creative projects. Fieldwork, however, is not expected at this level. Students are also expected to think very carefully about an appropriate scope of research and production plan for the proposed capstone. The project may also draw from academic coursework, relevant extracurricular activities or practical experience to support the research and realization of the project. At the end of the year, students present their work in a symposium for peers and the greater Fulbright community. Includes a major project building web interfaces to databases using PHP and MySQL. Introduction to NoSQL solutions. ### Question 27: Can Discrete Mathematics be counted for both Computer Science and Applied Mathematics majors?  
### Answer: 

No, Discrete Mathematics cannot be counted for both Computer Science and Applied Mathematics majors. According to the given information, students may not double count a course for two different requirements. Therefore, MATH 202 - Discrete Math can only count for either the Computer Science major or the Applied Mathematics major, but not both.

### Question 28: What steps should I take to ensure a smooth transfer of my exchange semester credits from Bard College to Fulbright?  
### Answer: 

To ensure a smooth transfer of your exchange semester credits from Bard College to Fulbright, you should follow these steps:

1. Review the Transfer Credit Policy V1.0 published in the One-Stop portal to understand the requirements and process.

2. Gather all necessary information about the courses you want to transfer, including course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments.

3. Submit an Application for Credit Transfer to the Office of the Registrar at Fulbright University Vietnam. You can send the official transcript with seal from Bard College directly to the Office of the Registrar at the email registrar@fulbright.edu.vn or the mailing address provided in the policy.

4. Ensure that the information you provide in the application is complete and correct, and sign the declaration stating that the information is accurate.

5. Wait for the Office of the Registrar to coordinate with the Office of the Dean to determine whether credit or an exemption is justified.

6. Follow up with the Office of the Registrar to check the status of your application and any additional information they might need. 

Remember that Fulbright will not evaluate transferable credit prior to acceptance, so make sure to submit your application after you have been accepted into Fulbright. Also, keep in mind that a maximum of 64 credit hours can be transferred and credited to a Fulbright undergraduate degree.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
courses delivered by Fulbright. When applying for Credit Transfer, a student is responsible for providing all the information that is requested about the course(s) for which they are applying to transfer. Information may include but not limited to course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments. To apply for Credit Transfer or an Exemption, students should submit an Application for Credit Transfer, along with the required information on the course(s), to the Office of the Registrar. The Registrar will coordinate with the Office of the Dean to determine whether credit or an exemption is justified. Credit Transfer from A-level, Advanced Placement (AP), International Baccalaureate (IB), and Cambridge International Exam (CIE) courses will be determined according to the AP/IB/CIE Credit Policy (in development). For more information, please refer to the Transfer Credit policy_Final_V3.0 published in the One Stop portal.

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
their Fulbright undergraduate degree. This is referred to as Credit Transfer. In addition, a student who has credit for a course passed at another university that is evaluated to be equivalent to a course at Fulbright may be given an Exemption from being required to do that Fulbright course. A maximum of 64 credit hours can be transferred and credited to a Fulbright undergraduate degree. That is, to earn a Fulbright University Vietnam undergraduate degree, a student must earn at least 64 credit hours from courses delivered by Fulbright. ### Question 29: Are 100-level and 200-level courses that are not explicitly categorized as E1, E2, E3, or E4 also excluded from fulfilling the Exploratory requirement?  
### Answer: 

Yes, 100-level and 200-level courses that are not explicitly categorized as E1, E2, E3, or E4 are also excluded from fulfilling the Exploratory requirement. The context specifies that students need to choose courses from the three categories: E1- Arts and Humanities, E2-Social Sciences, and STEM, and no course can be taken to fulfill more than one category. Therefore, only courses explicitly categorized within these three categories can be used to meet the Exploratory requirement. Courses not categorized as such do not count towards this requirement.

No course can be taken to fulfill more than one category. At most, 8 exploratory credits can be taken as Pass/No Pass. ### Question 31: If I withdraw from a course after the 4th week of the semester, will I be deducted 4 credits of financial aid?  
### Answer: 

Based on the information provided, if you withdraw from a course after the halfway point of the course (which is the end of week 4 for an 8-week course), you will receive a grade of 'F', which will affect your GPA. However, the information does not explicitly state that you will be deducted 4 credits of financial aid for doing so. Financial aid eligibility is mentioned as potentially being affected if course withdrawal results in fewer than the minimum credits for full-time enrollment, but it does not specify that you will be deducted 4 credits of financial aid for withdrawing after the 4th week. Therefore, the answer is that there is no direct statement indicating that you will be deducted 4 credits of financial aid for withdrawing after the 4th week.

### Question 32: Why do I need to take 8 exploratory courses?  
### Answer: 

You need to take 8 exploratory courses to step out of your comfort zone and explore broad areas of study. This helps you discover more fully where your interests and passions lie. These courses are designed to cover three main categories: E1- Arts and Humanities, E2-Social Sciences, and STEM. Each category requires you to complete 8 credits (2 courses at the 100-level or 200-level). No course can be taken to fulfill more than one category. Up to two of these 8 exploratory credits (2 courses) can be counted towards your major requirements. The goal is for you to complete these exploratory requirements by the end of your second year. However, it's important to note that class of 2023 students are exempted from this requirement. For classes of 2024, 2025, 2026, and 2027, there are additional categories: E3- Sciences and Engineering, and E4-Mathematics and Computing. Class of 2024 students need to complete 16 credits (4 courses) to fulfill their Exploratory requirements, one course from each category, with at most 4 out of 16 credits counted as Pass/No Pass. Students of classes of 2025, 2026, and 2027 need to complete 32 credits (8 courses), eight credits from each category.

### Question 33: Can I take 160 credits in 4 years given that I pay for the full tuition fee?  
### Answer: 

No, you cannot take 160 credits in 4 years. According to the provided context, Fulbright University Vietnam requires a minimum of 128 credit hours to graduate with an undergraduate degree. The typical full-time course load is 16 credit hours per term, meaning a student can accumulate up to 64 credit hours per academic year (assuming two terms per year). Therefore, it is not possible to take 160 credits in 4 years, as this exceeds the minimum graduation requirement and the typical full-time course load. Additionally, the payment of full tuition fees does not influence the number of credits you can take within the specified timeframe. It is important to adhere to the institution's guidelines regarding course loads and credit hours to ensure timely graduation.

STUDENT ENROLLMENT: 3.1 Course Load and Credit Hours Fulbright University Vietnam uses the “credit hour” as the quantum for course workload in the undergraduate program. A credit hour typically represents 3 hours of work during each week of a 16-week term. For a 4- credit hour course, a student would, therefore, be expected to put in 12 hours of work per week, including class time, for a total of 192 hours of work during a term. There are earned credits and attempted credits. Earned credits refer to the number of credit hours a student successfully completes with a grade of D or higher for letter grade options and a Pass for Pass/No Pass options. Attempted credits are the credit hours students enroll in and are recorded in the transcript, regardless of whether they complete the courses or pass them. This includes all courses for which a student receives a grade, including withdrawals (W), incompletes (I), repeats (RP), and failures (F). See section 4 for more details on different types of grades. To graduate

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
their Fulbright undergraduate degree. This is referred to as Credit Transfer. In addition, a student who has credit for a course passed at another university that is evaluated to be equivalent to a course at Fulbright may be given an Exemption from being required to do that Fulbright course. A maximum of 64 credit hours can be transferred and credited to a Fulbright undergraduate degree. That is, to earn a Fulbright University Vietnam undergraduate degree, a student must earn at least 64 credit hours from courses delivered by Fulbright. When applying for Credit Transfer, a student is responsible for providing all the information that is requested about the course(s) for which they are applying to transfer. Information may include but not limited to course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments. To apply for Credit Transfer or an Exemption, students should submit an Application for Credit Transfer, along with the required information on the course(s), to the Office of the Registrar.

### Question 34: What are the requirements for mathematics courses to pursue Human-Centered Engineering major?  
### Answer: 

To pursue a Human-Centered Engineering major, students must meet the following requirements regarding mathematics courses:

1. **Pure Mathematics Course**: Students are required to take at least 1 Pure mathematics course. Examples include Abstract Algebra and Real Analysis.

2. **Advanced Courses**: Students need to take at least 2 advanced courses. Examples include Advanced Statistics, Statistical Learning, Stochastic Calculus, Numerical Analysis, Optimization, and Partial Differential Equations.

3. **Applied Courses**: Students will have to take at least 2 applied courses (at least one at the 200 level). Examples include Game Theory, The Economics of Corruption, Money and Banking, Economics of Inequality, Economics of Education, Cost-Benefit Analysis, Market Design, Signal, Systems, and Control, Computer Vision, Introduction to Machine Learning, Algorithm, Statistical Learning, Introduction to AI, Operations Research, and Introduction to Quantitative Finance.

4. **Research Seminars**: Students should engage in research seminars to understand faculty's research, which could include topics like Optimization and Partial Differential Equations.

5. **Consultation with an Academic Advisor**: Course selection for advanced and elective courses requires consultation with an academic advisor.

6. **No Double Counting**: Students cannot double-count a course for two different requirements. For instance, Operations Research can only count for either 1 Advanced course or 1 Elective course, but not both.

These requirements ensure that students develop a strong foundation in pure mathematics, advanced mathematical concepts, practical applications, and research skills, all of which are crucial for a Human-Centered Engineering major. Additionally, students are encouraged to explore electives in Arts, Humanities, Social Sciences, and Entrepreneurship to complement their technical education. This holistic approach prepares students to address complex, real-world problems through innovative engineering solutions.

### Question 35: How is the grade of a replaced course displayed on the transcript? Will it replace the old one or create a new entry in the transcript?  
### Answer: 

The grade of a replaced course is displayed on the transcript such that the lower grade is overwritten by the notation "RP", meaning "repeated", and remains on the transcript. The higher grade is kept and used in the GPA calculation but does not replace the old entry. Therefore, the old grade entry still appears on the transcript along with the "RP" notation. This means that the replaced course creates a new entry in the transcript rather than replacing the old one.

### Question 36: What are the courses that can replace the capstone for a given major?  
### Answer: 

For the Information Systems (IS) major, if students choose not to do a capstone, they can replace it with 8 credits from IS courses, including at least 4 credits of 300-level course(s).  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
major or minor requirements must be taken for a letter grade. Students can claim a maximum of 8 credits (2 courses) toward both their Exploratory and major requirements. During their final year of study, students have the option to either complete a capstone project, which will count for 8 credits in their major area of study, or fulfill those credits with additional advanced coursework. Students pursuing a double major must complete all requirements for each major. If two majors (or two minors, or a major and a minor) share cross- listed or tagged1 courses, up to 8 credits (two courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements. This limit is per each pair of majors (or major and minor) and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim. For example, a student can major in both A and B and minor in C with a total of 6 double-counted courses: two in A and B, two in B and C, and two in A and C. This rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed or

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
opportunity to fulfill 8 credits of their major requirements via a capstone project. A student wishing to do a capstone must apply during the term prior to the first term of the capstone (Capstone I), and may only apply after having completed 80 credits of coursework. Students who do not do a capstone will need to fulfill 8 credits of coursework as specified in their major. Individual majors will determine eligibility requirements, and students should discuss their proposals with program coordinators and potential advisors to prepare their applications. Capstone projects will be graded No Pass/Pass/Honors and must be evaluated by the supervising faculty at least one month before the end of the student’s graduating term. ### Question 37: Is it possible to graduate with double majors in Human-Centered Engineering and Applied Mathematics? If yes, please provide a sample study plan.  
### Answer: 

Yes, it is possible to graduate with double majors in Human-Centered Engineering and Applied Mathematics. However, the provided context does not give specific information on how to structure a double major program or the exact overlap between the two majors' requirements.

To create a sample study plan, we would need to look at the specific course requirements for both majors. Generally, a student would need to complete all the required courses for both majors, ensuring no course is double-counted. 

For Applied Mathematics, the student needs to:
- Take at least 1 Pure Mathematics course.
- Take at least 2 Advanced courses.
- Take at least 2 Applied courses (at least one at 200 level).
- Take Research seminars.

For Human-Centered Engineering, the student needs to complete the core courses and electives specified by the program.

A sample study plan could look like this:

1. First Year:
   - Complete foundational courses in both majors.
   - Choose electives that can count towards both majors.

2. Second Year:
   - Continue foundational courses.
   - Start taking advanced courses in Applied Mathematics.
   - Begin taking specialized courses in Human-Centered Engineering.

3. Third Year:
   - Complete advanced courses in Applied Mathematics.
   - Take specialized courses in Human-Centered Engineering.
   - Start working on a capstone project or research in Applied Mathematics.

4. Fourth Year:
   - Complete remaining advanced courses in Applied Mathematics.
   - Finish specialized courses in Human-Centered Engineering.
   - Work on the capstone project or research in Human-Centered Engineering.
   - Take any remaining courses to fulfill the requirements for both majors.

This is a simplified example and actual planning should be done in consultation with advisors from both departments to ensure all requirements are met without double counting courses. The exact courses and sequence might vary depending on the specific curriculum of each major.

For example, an exploratory course can also be counted as a major course for the corresponding major. However, the number of double-counted credits is often limited (e.g., see subsections 13.2 and 13.3). Additionally, any particular course can only be used to satisfy at most two requirements. For instance, if course X is cross-listed between major A and major B and tagged by minor C, then X can be used to fulfill the requirements of major A and major B, or major A and minor C, or major B and minor C. Triple counting is not allowed. 13.9  Maximal Length of Study Fulbright follows MOET regulations, which state that the maximum time to complete the program cannot exceed double the standard

### Question 40: What actions are considered plagiarism? Are AI-generated works counted?  
### Answer: 

Presenting text, images, or other content created by others or by generative AI as your own work, even at the sentence level, is considered plagiarism and grounds for failure of Capstone I and/or Capstone II. Yes, AI-generated works are included in this consideration. Therefore, it is essential to document the use of generative AI comprehensively to highlight the originality and human contributions to the project. This includes clearly defining the reasons for utilizing generative AI, specifying the AI tools, models, or platforms employed, outlining the process and methodology, and addressing ethical and copyright issues associated with using generative AI. Transparency and proper documentation are crucial to avoid any accusations of plagiarism.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: VIETNAM STUDIES CAPSTONE GUIDELINES.pdf, Page: 6]
Clearly deﬁne the reasons for utilizing generative AI and the speciﬁc elements of the project it contributes to. • Tools and Platforms: Specify the AI tools, models, or platforms employed. • Process and Methodology: Outline how AI will be incorporated, detailing which aspects of the project will be generated, improved, or altered with the use of AI. • Ethical and Copyright Issues: Address the ethical and copyright concerns associated with using generative AI and how these will be addressed throughout the project. This comprehensive documentation promotes transparency, oﬀers insight into AI's role in the creative process, and highlights the originality and human contributions to the project. 1.8. ### Question 41: Why is the graduation requirement 128 credits, but the major requirement is only 48 credits?  
### Answer: 

The graduation requirement is 128 credits because it includes all the institutional requirements, which extend beyond just the major requirements. The major requirement being 56 credits refers specifically to the courses needed to complete the major itself, while the 128 credit total encompasses a broader educational experience including general education courses, electives, and possibly other requirements such as experiential learning or capstone projects. Therefore, the major requirement is a subset of the overall graduation requirement.

Students pursuing a double major must complete all requirements for each major. If two majors (or two minors, or a major and a minor) share cross- listed or tagged1 courses, up to 8 credits (two courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements. This limit is per each pair of majors (or major and minor) and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim. ### Question 42: Explain the cross-listed mechanism between courses.  
### Answer: 

The cross-listed mechanism between courses is a system where two or more courses with different course IDs but similar content and learning objectives are offered simultaneously. Students can enroll in any of these courses and receive credit for one of them, as they cover the same material. This allows for flexibility in scheduling and accommodating different student needs and preferences. The courses may be taught by different instructors, but they will have the same prerequisites and grading policies. It's important to note that while the courses are cross-listed, they are distinct entities with their own unique course IDs. Therefore, students should check the specific requirements and offerings before enrolling.

### Question 44: How does the core quest course selection work to fulfill core credits?  
### Answer: 

To fulfill core credits through the QUEST (Quantitative Understanding and Empirical Scientific Thinking) course selection, students must complete one course from this core group. The core group consists of four courses: Quantitative Reasoning for a Digital Age (4 credits), Scientific Inquiry (4 credits), Introduction to Statistics (4 credits), and Programming for Data Science and Visualization (4 credits). These courses are pre-assigned to students during their first year or the first semester of their second year. Therefore, students do not have the option to choose which course within the QUEST group they take; it is predetermined for them. This ensures that all students receive a foundational education in quantitative reasoning, scientific inquiry, statistics, and programming for data science and visualization, which are essential skills for many academic and professional fields. For Class of 2027 students and earlier, these four courses together contribute to the total of five core courses required for 20 credits. For Class of 2023 students, who are exempt from the Exploratory requirements, the same core courses apply but without the additional Exploratory requirements.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]

### Question 45: Can I take a 300-level course to fulfill a 200-level major requirement?  
### Answer: 

Yes, until the university offers a robust list of 200 and 300-Level Courses, students can satisfy the 48 Credits with any combination of 200 and 300 Level Courses. Therefore, taking a 300-level course to fulfill a 200-level major requirement is acceptable. However, it's recommended to follow the above requirements when selecting courses where possible.

major or minor requirements must be taken for a letter grade. Students can claim a maximum of 8 credits (2 courses) toward both their Exploratory and major requirements. During their final year of study, students have the option to either complete a capstone project, which will count for 8 credits in their major area of study, or fulfill those credits with additional advanced coursework. Students pursuing a double major must complete all requirements for each major. If two majors (or two minors, or a major and a minor) share cross- listed or tagged1 courses, up to 8 credits (two courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements. This limit is per each pair of majors (or major and minor) and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim. For example, a student can major in both A and B and minor in C with a total of 6 double-counted courses: two in A and B, two in B and C, and two in A and C. ### Question 46: If I take a course at another university and want to transfer the credits to Fulbright, but Fulbright doesn’t have that major code, yet the course is related to a major at Fulbright, can I count it toward that major?  
### Answer: 

No, you cannot count the course toward that major if Fulbright does not have the major code for that course. The policy states that a student can apply to have credit counted towards their Fulbright undergraduate degree through Credit Transfer, but this is only applicable if the course at another university is equivalent to a course at Fulbright. If Fulbright does not have the major code for that course, it means the course is not recognized as equivalent to any course at Fulbright, and thus, the credits cannot be transferred or exempted for that major. You would need to take the equivalent course offered at Fulbright to fulfill your major requirements.

All students for whom English is not their first language must take an English Assessment Test required by NECHE Accreditation. 13.8  Double Counting In satisfying degree requirements, some courses can be double-counted. For example, an exploratory course can also be counted as a major course for the corresponding major. However, the number of double-counted credits is often limited (e.g., see subsections 13.2 and 13.3). Additionally, any particular course can only be used to satisfy at most two requirements. For instance, if course X is cross-listed between major A and major B and tagged by minor C, then X can be used to fulfill the requirements of major A and major B, or major A and minor C, or major B and minor C. Triple counting is not allowed. 13.9  Maximal Length of Study Fulbright follows MOET regulations, which state that the maximum time to complete the program cannot exceed double the standard

### Question 47: I have 112 credits from Fulbright and 16 credits from EL. Can I graduate?  
### Answer: 

Based on the information provided, you need a minimum of 128 credit hours to graduate with an undergraduate degree from Fulbright. You currently have 128 credits from Fulbright and 16 credits from EL, which totals 144 credits. Therefore, yes, you can graduate. However, it's important to ensure that these credits meet the specific requirements of your major and any other applicable requirements such as electives and the capstone project. It would also be advisable to consult with your academic advisor to confirm that all requirements are met.

Fulbright’s Experiential Learning Program (ELP) exists to create, standardize, and facilitate academic credit-bearing experiential learning experiences. All full-time, undergraduate, degree- seeking students must complete at least 04 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the ELP as a graduation requirement. Current ELP streams are housed within Academic Affairs (AA), Career Services (CS), and Center for Entrepreneurship and Innovation (CEI), where each team is responsible for administrative and academic duties of their respective stream(s). The ELP operates within Fulbright’s undergraduate program’s standard operating procedures and is developed in consultation with undergraduate program leadership and faculty. For more details, please refer here https://onestop.fulbright.edu.vn/s/article/Experiential-Learning- Program 13.5  Electives To complete the degree, students are free to take elective courses from the Course Catalogue. ### Question 48: I have received an offer to attend an international conference but lack funding. What school funds can I apply for?  
### Answer: 

You can apply for funding from FUV's student research fund, which supports student's research projects, including capstone. This fund might be applicable for attending an international conference if it contributes to your studies and research. Make sure to check the eligibility criteria and application process for this fund. Additionally, you can explore applying for funding from other external sources. Discussing with your advisor and the Psychology faculty can also provide guidance on securing the necessary resources for your participation in the conference.

### Question 49: What is the maximum number of credits I can transfer from another university after officially enrolling at Fulbright?  
### Answer: 

The maximum number of credits you can transfer from another university after officially enrolling at Fulbright is 64 credit hours. This means that to earn a Fulbright University Vietnam undergraduate degree, a student must earn at least 64 credit hours from courses delivered by Fulbright. However, it's important to note that this does not include the total number of credits needed to graduate, which is 128 credit hours. The 64 credit hours are part of the 128 credit hours requirement, with the remaining 64 credit hours needing to be earned from Fulbright courses.

### Question 50: In a regular semester, can I take only 2 courses? If so, how will my tuition fees be affected?  
### Answer: 

No, you cannot take only 2 courses in a regular semester. According to the guidelines provided, students are required to register for no fewer than 12 credit hours and no more than 16 credit hours per term. To take fewer than 12 credit hours, you would need to submit a "Petition for Alternative Course Load" form to the Registrar's Office, which must be approved by your Academic/Major Advisor.

Regarding tuition fees, there is no mention of a reduction in tuition for students who take fewer than 12 academic credits. Therefore, taking only 2 courses would likely result in higher tuition costs compared to taking the standard full-time course load of 16 credit hours. However, if you are experiencing exceptional circumstances, such as illness or medical conditions, you might be able to reduce your course load with proper documentation and approval. In such cases, tuition credit might be considered, but this is not guaranteed and would depend on the specifics of your situation and the approval process. It's important to consult with your Academic/Major Advisor and the Registrar's Office to explore your options.

### Question 51: Can I pursue 3 majors?  
### Answer: 

According to the information provided, you can major in multiple subjects, but there are specific rules regarding how many majors you can pursue simultaneously and how credits can be shared between them.

The text states that "Students pursuing a double major must complete all requirements for each major." This implies that pursuing three majors would require completing all the requirements for each of the three majors. However, it does not explicitly mention the possibility of pursuing three majors. 

Additionally, the text mentions that "If two majors (or two minors, or a major and a minor) share cross-listed or tagged courses, up to 8 credits (two courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements." This rule applies to pairs of majors or a major and a minor. It does not provide any information about pursuing three majors.

Therefore, while it is possible to pursue two majors, the information provided does not explicitly allow for pursuing three majors. You would need to check the institution's official policies or speak with an academic advisor to confirm whether pursuing three majors is possible. Based on the given information, it seems that pursuing three majors might not be feasible due to the lack of specific rules allowing for this scenario.

### Question 52: How can I change my major declaration?  
### Answer: 

You can change your major declaration by following the procedures outlined in the additional policies and requirements section of your major's description, flowchart, or handbook. Any exceptions to these procedures must be approved by the major coordinator and the Dean's Office. The process typically involves submitting a formal request to the academic advisor or the Dean's Office, providing justification for the change, and possibly completing any required prerequisite courses. It's important to consult the specific guidelines for your intended major to ensure compliance with all necessary requirements. If you're experiencing initial academic difficulties, you may need to address those issues before changing your major. In cases of illness or medical conditions, a letter from a licensed medical doctor is required, detailing the medical problem, treatment, and when the student may resume full-time coursework. For other reasons, a recommendation from the academic advisor or Dean's Office may be necessary. Always check the official university policies for the most accurate and up-to-date information.

### Question 53: What is the process of delaying my payment?  
### Answer: 

The process of requesting a late and/or an extension of tuition fee payment involves contacting Student Financial Services. They will try to understand the circumstances and request a timely response from you. If you anticipate being unable to clear the balance on time, you should meet with the Student Financial Services team as soon as possible to discuss alternative solutions. This process does not allow you to register for new courses or participate in classes or a Work-Study Program until your outstanding balance is cleared. If you do not resolve the issue within the given period, you might be placed on Administrative Leave of Absence for up to one term. Remember, it's important to communicate with them early to avoid any disruption to your studies.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 15]
Student Financial Services to request a late and/or an extension of tuition fee payment. Before placing a student in this type of absence, the Student Financial Services team will attempt to determine the circumstances and request a timely response from the student. With this absence status, students are unable to register for new course(s) during the registration period, participate in classes or a Work-Study Program in the current term. A student will only be reinstated as “Active” status if the outstanding balance is clear. If the student anticipates being unable to clear the account on time, the student should meet with the Student Financial Services team as soon as possible to request assistance and alternative solutions. After the approved period of absence, a student is put on Administrative Leave of Absence (Admin LOA) for a maximum of one term if the Registrar’s Office receives no response of return confirmation or no registration in the returning term. After one term of Admin LOA, a student is

### Question 59: If I'm going for a double major then how many courses can be double count maximum?  
### Answer: 

If you're going for a double major, the maximum number of courses that can be double-counted is 8 credits (2 courses) per pair of majors. This means that for each combination of two majors, you can use up to 8 credits towards fulfilling the requirements for both. So, if you have two majors, the maximum double-counted courses would be 8 credits. However, this limit applies to each pair of majors separately, and it does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits across all your majors. For example, you could major in both A and B and minor in C with a total of 6 double-counted courses: two in A and B, two in B and C, and two in A and C. This rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed or tagged.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
major or minor requirements must be taken for a letter grade. Students can claim a maximum of 8 credits (2 courses) toward both their Exploratory and major requirements. During their final year of study, students have the option to either complete a capstone project, which will count for 8 credits in their major area of study, or fulfill those credits with additional advanced coursework. Students pursuing a double major must complete all requirements for each major. If two majors (or two minors, or a major and a minor) share cross- listed or tagged1 courses, up to 8 credits (two courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements. This limit is per each pair of majors (or major and minor) and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim. For example, a student can major in both A and B and minor in C with a total of 6 double-counted courses: two in A and B, two in B and C, and two in A and C. This rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed or

### Question 60: Can you give me the grade translation from alphabetic to numerical?  
### Answer: 

The grade translation from alphabetic to numerical at Fulbright is as follows:

- A: 4.0
- A-: 3.7
- C-: 1.7

These values represent the grade points assigned to each letter grade within the specified percentage ranges. Note that these scales may vary for individual courses if decided by the respective faculty. For other letter grades not mentioned, they would fall into the remaining categories outside of the provided ranges.

### Question 62: Why and how am I getting academic suspension?  
### Answer: 

You are getting academic suspension because your academic performance has put you at risk of losing the opportunity to study at Fulbright, either temporarily or permanently. Specifically, if you are on Academic Probation and fail to meet all the requirements of your Learning Contract, you may be placed on Academic Suspension. The process involves meeting with the Dean’s Office, who will establish the conditions you need to meet before returning to Fulbright. During your suspension, you may not visit the Fulbright campus without permission from the Dean’s Office or the Vice President of Student Affairs for relevant meetings. Suspensions typically last for one term or one academic year, and you can only be suspended a maximum of two times. If you are suspended a third time, your enrollment in the program will be canceled, and you will need to apply for re-admission, providing a letter explaining the reasons for your suspensions and the measures you have taken to address them. The re-admission decision will be made by the Dean’s Office in consultation with the appropriate members of faculty and staff.

### Question 63: How does the P/NP grade work?  
### Answer: 

The P/NP (Pass/No Pass) grading system allows students to take up to 8 credits in one academic year on a Pass/No Pass basis. To do so, they must submit a Petition to Elect Pass/No Pass Grade form to the Registrar's Office before 4:00 PM on Friday of Week 4 of the term. 

Once a student converts a course grade option to Pass/No Pass, the grade option cannot be changed back. A grade of 'C-' or higher will be counted as a Pass, which means the course can be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. However, any grade below a 'C-' will be counted as a No Pass, and no credit will be granted for this result.

It's important to note that Pass/No Pass grades do not apply to core courses and cannot be used to count toward major/minor requirements. The Registrar's Office is responsible for converting the final grade to P/NP after receiving the final grade submission by the instructor at the end of the term. Additionally, grades 'D' or 'D+' can only be counted toward the requirements for elective courses. If a student fails to complete all remaining course work within the agreed-upon timeframe, typically not exceeding 6 months from the end of the course, an incomplete grade of 'I' may be awarded temporarily. Otherwise, the student will receive a No Pass grade.

### Question 64: How many courses can I take as P/NP at maximum and how will it contribute to the official transcript GPA?  
### Answer: 

You can take a maximum of 2 courses as P/NP at once, which typically amounts to 8 credits in one academic year. Courses graded with a Pass (P) will be shown on the Official Transcript but will not contribute to the official transcript GPA. Courses graded with a No Pass (NP) will also be shown on the Official Transcript and will not contribute to the official transcript GPA. Therefore, neither Pass nor No Pass grades will affect your official transcript GPA. Only courses graded with letter grades (A-F) will be included in the GPA calculation.

### Question 66: What and how do I get an Academic Warning?  
### Answer: 

To receive an Academic Warning, you must not be making satisfactory progress towards your degree and/or fall below a 2.0 GPA, or for other reasons such as failure of attendance, participation, citizenship, or academic integrity. An Academic Warning is sent out by the Registrar’s Office. You are required to attend an Academic Progress Meeting where a Learning Contract will be created with specific conditions tailored to your individual situation. The Registrar's Office will be informed as a matter of record and follow-up. If you receive three official warnings, it could result in Disciplinary Action, constituting Academic Probation or Academic Suspension.

ACADEMIC STANDING: Academic standing refers to how well a Fulbright student is meeting the general expectations toward the fulfillment of their degree. There are four categories of academic standing. 6.1 Good Standing Students with a minimum of 2.0 GPA, who are not on academic or non- academic warning, probation, suspension, or dismissal, and who are in good standing financially, are considered in Good Standing. Only students in Good Standing may participate in off-campus programs and other opportunities as specified. 6.2 Academic Warning This is usually the first level of intervention for students who are not making satisfactory progress toward their degree and/or who fall below a 2.0 GPA, or for other reasons such as failure of attendance, participation, citizenship, or academic integrity. An Academic Warning is sent out by the Registrar’s Office. The student is required to attend an Academic Progress Meeting during which a Learning Contract will be created with specific conditions tailored to the

### Question 67: How can I make reservations of rooms for personal usage?  
### Answer: 

You cannot stay on campus & residence during a period of absence from your studies normally. The exception will be considered case by case. Therefore, making reservations of rooms for personal usage during your leave of absence might not be possible unless you get special permission and it is approved on a case-by-case basis. For further inquiries, please contact Residential Life Staff.

### Question 68: Can you provide me with some courses suggestion to take to major in Math?  
### Answer: 

Based on the provided context, here are some suggested courses to major in Math:

**Foundation Courses (100 level):**
- Linear Algebra
- Single Variable Calculus
- Introduction to Statistics
- Multivariable Calculus

**Intermediate Courses (200 level):**
- Probability
- Differential Equations
- Discrete Mathematics
- Numerical Analysis

**Advanced Courses (300 level):**
- Advanced Statistics
- Statistical Learning
- Stochastic Calculus
- Numerical Analysis
- Optimization
- Partial Differential Equations

**Elective Applied Courses:**
- Game Theory (from Economics)
- Signal, Systems, and Control (from Engineering)
- Introduction to Machine Learning (from Computer Science)
- Operations Research (from Applied Mathematics)
- Introduction to Quantitative Finance (from Applied Mathematics)

Remember, consultation with an academic advisor is required for course selection, especially for choosing advanced courses. Also, note that students may not double count a course for two different requirements. For instance, Operations Research can only count for either 1 Advanced or 1 Applied course requirement. 

Good luck with your studies!

Using a student-centered, interdisciplinary, and future-focused approach, the Computer Science major aims to educate the next generation of local leaders who will make a meaningful and lasting societal impact both in Vietnam – one of the most quickly emerging and innovative technology economies in the world – and beyond. As part of the major, students will be equipped with the foundational knowledge in Computer Science and relevant disciplines. ### Question 70: I'm currently under a General Work Program for Experiential Learning but the company do not pay me in any form. How can I get the subsidy from Fulbright University?  
### Answer: 

Based on the information provided in the context, there is no mention of subsidies being provided by Fulbright University for unpaid internships or experiential learning programs. The Fulbright's Experiential Learning Program (ELP) focuses on creating, standardizing, and facilitating academic credit-bearing experiential learning experiences, but it does not appear to provide financial subsidies for companies that do not pay interns. You should check directly with Fulbright's academic advisors or the relevant department overseeing the ELP to inquire about potential alternative arrangements or additional resources that might be available. They can provide guidance tailored to your specific situation. It's also advisable to review the latest policies and procedures related to the ELP as they may have been updated since the last version of the document you referenced.

Fulbright’s Experiential Learning Program (ELP) exists to create, standardize, and facilitate academic credit-bearing experiential learning experiences. All full-time, undergraduate, degree- seeking students must complete at least 04 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the ELP as a graduation requirement. Current ELP streams are housed within Academic Affairs (AA), Career Services (CS), and Center for Entrepreneurship and Innovation (CEI), where each team is responsible for administrative and academic duties of their respective stream(s). The ELP operates within Fulbright’s undergraduate program’s standard operating procedures and is developed in consultation with undergraduate program leadership and faculty.
