### Question 71: Can you give me the process of making a Capstone for graduation?  
### Answer: 

The process of making a capstone for graduation involves several key steps. First, you need to meet with your advisor as early as possible to set up a regular meeting schedule and establish expectations for submissions along with timelines. This initial meeting helps to outline the scope and direction of your capstone project.

Next, you will start working on various components of your capstone, such as a literature review or annotated bibliography, which should be at least five pages (2,000 words). Additionally, you will prepare an introduction and possibly other materials or documents that are agreed upon with your advisors. These could include things like questionnaires, depending on the nature of your project.

As you progress through the semester, you'll continue to refine these elements under the guidance of your advisor. By the end of the term, you will submit a comprehensive end-of-term submission that demonstrates your successful progress towards completing the capstone. This final submission should showcase your original critical and creative thinking and may include the literature review, introduction, and any other agreed-upon materials.

In Capstone II, you will then focus more on the production phase of your project, whether that means writing your thesis or creating a piece of art or media. Throughout this process, ongoing communication with your advisor is crucial to ensure that you stay on track and meet all necessary requirements for a high-quality capstone.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Art & Media Studies Capstone Handbook _v3_210125.pdf, Page: 6]
1. General Information: A culmination to the student’s curriculum, the capstone is an individual project that demonstrates the principal learning outcomes and competencies of that curriculum in a meaningful and coherent way. The capstone may also draw from relevant extra-curricular activities and practical experience to support the research and realization of the project. The capstone should evidence competency in a primary disciplinary specialization (optionally supported by secondary and tertiary disciplinary areas). In the Art & Media Studies major, the capstone could take the form of a thesis, an art work, or a film. For other kinds of projects, please consult with your prospective advisor(s) early in your junior year to determine the suitability and feasibility of your proposed project. Remember, the capstone should demonstrate original critical and creative thinking, and we encourage primary research. However, it should not require extensive fieldwork. You should think very carefully about an

### Question 72: What are the grades required to get a distinctive graduation?  
### Answer: 

To get a distinctive graduation, a student needs to achieve a capstone graded as Honors. According to the grading rubrics provided, an 'A' or equivalent grade point would be required to receive an Honors grade for the capstone project. This would lead to Graduation with Honors.

### Question 73: How can I graduate with Honor or lie within the top GPA?  
### Answer: 

To graduate with honors or maintain a high GPA, you need to achieve a minimum GPA of 3.5 as per the eligibility criteria mentioned. This GPA requirement is crucial for capstone applicants who aim to earn honors for their capstone projects. It's important to consistently perform well academically throughout your studies, especially during your senior year if you're planning to earn honors for the capstone. Maintaining this GPA ensures that you meet the academic standards set for earning honors. Any drop below this GPA could result in the capstone being capped at pass instead of honors. Therefore, focus on excelling in your coursework and managing your grades effectively to graduate with honors.

Students may repeat a course if they have received a grade of ‘D+’, ‘D’, ‘F’, or NP for the course or have withdrawn and received a grade of ‘W’. Advising process Successful applicants will be matched to their first choice of primary and secondary advisor where possible. If the student’s first or second preference cannot be accommodated due to the necessity of maintaining a fair distribution of faculty workload, the major capstone coordinator will consult with the student to determine an appropriate solution. The primary advisor is your first point of contact and should hold expertise relevant to your project, for example, in terms of being a specialist in the project’s disciplinary field. The primary advisor may also be your academic advisor in the major. They will be the primary reviewer of your work in  

</details> 

### Question 74: How many courses can I take with P/NP grade in total?  
### Answer: 

You can take a total of 2 courses with a Pass/No Pass grade in one academic year. This is based on the information provided in the context, which states that "take a total of 8 credits (typically 2 courses, 4 credits each) in one academic year on a Pass/No Pass basis". Therefore, you can take up to 2 courses with a P/NP grade in total during an academic year.

### Answer: 

There are four types of absences mentioned in the given context. These include general absences, military leave, excused absence due to university-sponsored events/activities, and emergency absences. Each type has specific conditions and procedures outlined for students to follow.

### Question 76: How many types of leave of absence are there and how can I have one?  
### Answer: 

There are three types of leave of absence: Personal Leave, Medical Leave, and Administrative Leave of Absence. To have one, you need to fill out the Undergraduate Leave of Absence form, consult with your Academic Advisor, and submit the form before the last day of class. Make sure you meet the eligibility criteria and follow the procedures as outlined in the Academic Policy, section Leave of Absence. Additionally, you may need to provide supporting documents depending on the type of leave you're applying for.

Students may return earlier to Fulbright by notifying the Registrar’s Office at least eight (08) weeks in advance of the returning term. ### Question 79: What is the school's policy on academic dishonesty, and how are violations handled?  
### Answer: 

The school's policy on academic dishonesty, particularly regarding the capstone project, is governed by Fulbright University Vietnam's Code of Academic Integrity. Violations of this code are subject to specific regulations and handling procedures outlined within the code. These measures aim to ensure academic honesty and integrity throughout the educational process. Any substantive changes to this policy are reviewed annually and require approval from the Dean’s Office and the Provost before being published and made available through the One Stop portal. This ensures that the policy remains current and effective in addressing academic integrity issues. For group projects and other academic activities, there may be additional policies or guidelines that complement the Code of Academic Integrity. However, the primary reference for academic dishonesty in the context of the capstone project is the aforementioned Code of Academic Integrity. Irrelevant references such as IRB approval and grading processes are not directly related to handling academic dishonesty.

### Question 80: What are the policies regarding retaking exams or improving grades?  
### Answer: 

The policies regarding retaking exams or improving grades are as follows:

1. Students are required to repeat core courses if they receive a grade of 'F' and/or courses counted toward major/minor if they receive a grade below 'C-'.

2. Students may repeat a course if they have received a grade of 'D+', 'D', 'F', or NP for the course, or have withdrawn and received a grade of 'W'.

3. In special cases, a student may request to repeat a course after having received a grade higher than a 'D+' following consultation with the student's academic/major advisor, the course instructor, and the Registrar's Office. Considerations will include course availability and capacity in the next academic term or next academic year.

4. A higher grade will be kept and used in the GPA calculation. The lower grade will be overwritten by the notation "RP", meaning "repeated", and remain on the transcript.

5. Credits of the repeated course are counted toward the total attempted credits.

6. A student may not retake the same course for the third time unless they failed the second time or if a specific grade is needed to meet the major requirements.

7. Students shall consult with their Academic/Major Advisor about their program plan if they are considering taking the class for a third time.

These policies aim to ensure that students have opportunities to improve their grades while maintaining academic integrity and fairness.

APPEALS: A student who wishes to dispute a final grade in a course should first discuss the matter with the course instructor(s). If the matter remains unresolved and the student believes there has been an error in grading, bias, or failure to follow published grading policies, the student may file an appeal as follows: • Submit the Review of Final Grade Request form to the Registrar's Office within five (05) business days from the date on which the Registrar's Office posts the final grade for the term. • The Registrar's Office informs the Dean’s Office of the case. After investigation, if the Deans can mediate, no further action is required. Otherwise, the Registrar's Office organizes a panel review with the Dean’s Office for an independent evaluation of the grade. The grade determined after this evaluation shall be the final grade. In cases concerning the interpretation of a course policy, the Dean’s Office will defer to the course syllabus whenever possible and otherwise will make a final ruling on the

### Question 81: How does the university accommodate students with chronic illnesses or personal emergencies that affect attendance?  
### Answer: 

The university accommodates students with chronic illnesses or personal emergencies that affect attendance through recognizing exceptional circumstances. These circumstances include exceptional medical conditions such as hospitalization or incapacitation due to injury, illness, or mental health crises. Additionally, close bereavement, being a victim of a serious crime, disabilities for which reasonable adjustments are not yet in place, and unforeseeable transport difficulties are also considered. For these situations, students are responsible for submitting appropriate documentation and contacting their instructors to initiate arrangements to make up any missed work. Approval from the Office of the Dean and Deans of Students is required for trips during the term. Students must be in good academic standing and not on probation to be excused from the class. The university encourages instructors to outline attendance expectations at the beginning of each term and to allow students to make up missed assignments if the absence is reasonable. They are also expected to inform students if they are in danger of failing the course due to class absence or missed assignments. A course withdrawal or an Incomplete grade may be pursued if appropriate under the University policies. Students are encouraged to request permission to be absent at least 24 hours prior to class time, except in exceptional circumstances. They should discuss any unplanned absence or known conflicts with the course instructor(s) as soon as possible and make all late assignment submissions approved by the course instructor according to the instructions. The university and instructor(s) are encouraged to accommodate students for university-sponsored events/activities for academic, non-academic, and recognized student organizations. However, excused absence due to university-sponsored events/activities requires a University Official Activity Excused Absence Request Form submitted to the Dean’s Office, keeping Academic Affairs and Registrar’s Office informed for the record. Only faculty or supervising staff can request the Excused Absence for university-sponsored events/activities.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 17]
EXCEPTIONAL CIRCUMSTANCES: The University acknowledges that sometimes a student will experience circumstances that will impact their ability to fulfill the expectations of the University, including but not limited to assessment, attendance, and paying fees. Circumstances that may fall into this category are: • Exceptional medical circumstances, e.g., hospitalization or incapacitation through injury, illness, or mental health crisis. • Close bereavement, e.g., partner, child, parent, sibling, grandparent, and grandchild. Housemates or very close friends may also be considered as ‘close’, though evidence of the relationship may be required. • Victim of a serious crime • Disabilities for which reasonable adjustments are not yet in place and where the delay is not due to the student • Exceptional and unforeseeable transport difficulties e.g., major transport incidents, cancelled flights. This does not include everyday issues, e.g., traffic congestion, missed buses or trains. • Legal proceedings requiring

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 13]

### Question 82: Are students allowed to use AI tools like ChatGPT for assignments? If so, under what conditions?  
### Answer: 

Students are allowed to use AI tools like ChatGPT for assignments, but under specific conditions. They must provide full documentation of its usage, clearly defining the reasons for utilizing generative AI and the specific elements of the project it contributes to. This includes specifying the AI tools, models, or platforms employed, outlining how AI will be incorporated, and addressing ethical and copyright concerns associated with using generative AI. By doing so, students promote transparency, offer insight into AI's role in the creative process, and highlight the originality and human contributions to the project. It is important to note that failure to obtain IRB approval could result in delays to the project and/or its suspension. Therefore, students are advised to begin their IRB application as soon as their Capstone application is accepted, or during Capstone I at the latest. More information on the IRB approval process can be found at the provided link.  

<details>

### Question 83: Where can I get support for mental health treatment?  
### Answer: 

You can seek support for mental health treatment through various resources and programs mentioned in the context, such as the Mental Health First Aid Training Program, Community Survey on Mental Health Needs, Public Art Project on Mental Health Themes, Resource Guide for Local Mental Health Services, and Therapeutic Gardening or Nature Program. These initiatives aim to address mental health needs within the community and provide guidance and support for those seeking mental health treatment. However, it is important to consult with healthcare professionals for personalized advice and treatment options. The Capstone by Applied Project also includes an Evaluation Report that demonstrates the project's relevance to psychological principles and its impact on mental health, which can be valuable for understanding the effectiveness of different approaches.

### Question 85: Where can I find resources to facilitate my graduate program after Fulbright undergraduate?  
### Answer: 

You can find resources to facilitate your graduate program after Fulbright undergraduate by leveraging the learning outcomes and program educational objectives (PEOs) outlined in the Fulbright University Vietnam document. Specifically, PEO1 aims to equip students with the necessary skills and knowledge to gain employment in industry or to study in graduate schools. Additionally, PEO2 focuses on instilling a strong code of professional and personal ethics, along with effective collaboration and communication skills, which are crucial for success in graduate programs. Furthermore, PEO3 emphasizes cultivating students into innovators and thinkers capable of solving challenges, a skill set highly valued in advanced academic pursuits. These resources, combined with the specific disciplinary focus, language and interpersonal skills gained through the Fulbright Vietnam Studies program, will prepare you well for graduate-level studies. Moreover, the document mentions that Fulbright graduates are prepared for graduate programs with a specific focus on Vietnam and related fields in universities around the world, providing additional support and opportunities for further education. Lastly, the learning outcomes of recognizing the importance of historical, cultural, and regional contexts can enhance your analytical and critical thinking skills, making you a competitive candidate for various graduate programs.

### Question 89: I used to take an undergraduate program at another university and I want to transfer credit of studied courses at that university. What should I do?  
### Answer: 

To transfer credit for the courses you studied at another university, you need to follow these steps:

1. Gather all the necessary information about the courses you want to transfer, such as the course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments.

2. Submit an Application for Credit Transfer to the Office of the Registrar at Fulbright University Vietnam.

3. Ensure that you provide all the requested information about the courses for which you are applying to transfer.

4. The Office of the Registrar will coordinate with the Office of the Dean to determine whether credit or an exemption is justified based on the information provided.

5. If your request is approved, the course(s) approved for transfer credit will be updated in your Official Transcript under the "Transfer Credit" section in the following term by the Office of the Registrar.

By following these steps, you can successfully transfer credit for the courses you studied at another university towards your Fulbright undergraduate degree.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
courses delivered by Fulbright. When applying for Credit Transfer, a student is responsible for providing all the information that is requested about the course(s) for which they are applying to transfer. Information may include but not limited to course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments. To apply for Credit Transfer or an Exemption, students should submit an Application for Credit Transfer, along with the required information on the course(s), to the Office of the Registrar. The Registrar will coordinate with the Office of the Dean to determine whether credit or an exemption is justified. Credit Transfer from A-level, Advanced Placement (AP), International Baccalaureate (IB), and Cambridge International Exam (CIE) courses will be determined according to the AP/IB/CIE Credit Policy (in development). For more information, please refer to the Transfer Credit policy_Final_V3.0 published in the One Stop portal.

### Question 90: What are the policies of CWP?  
### Answer: 

The policies of CWP, as described in the given context, pertain to passing grades and their corresponding percentages. Specifically, it states that a grade of 1.7 or higher passes at a rate of 70-72.9%. There are additional requirements and exceptions for majors and minors, which means that specific policies might vary depending on the major or minor. However, any exceptions to these policies need to be approved by the major coordinator and the Dean's Office. The context also mentions other grading categories like "Fair" (grades between 73-76.9%) but does not provide further details about CWP policies beyond the passing grade criteria. Therefore, the primary policy discussed here is the passing grade requirement and its associated percentage range.

### Question 91: I'm a student athlete then how can I bypass all of physical education courses required to graduate?  
### Answer: 

As a student athlete, you typically cannot bypass the physical education courses required to graduate. These courses are mandatory for all students and do not count toward the 128-credit requirement. Therefore, you would still need to complete them as part of your graduation requirements. However, you might want to check with your athletic department or academic advisor for any specific policies or exemptions they might offer.

All students for whom English is not their first language must take an English Assessment Test required by NECHE Accreditation. 13.8  Double Counting In satisfying degree requirements, some courses can be double-counted. For example, an exploratory course can also be counted as a major course for the corresponding major. However, the number of double-counted credits is often limited (e.g., see subsections 13.2 and 13.3). Additionally, any particular course can only be used to satisfy at most two requirements. For instance, if course X is cross-listed between major A and major B and tagged by minor C, then X can be used to fulfill the requirements of major A and major B, or major A and minor C, or major B and minor C. Triple counting is not allowed. 13.9  Maximal Length of Study Fulbright follows MOET regulations, which state that the maximum time to complete the program cannot exceed double the standard

### Question 92: I'm currently a third year student and moved out of university dormitory after first year but now I'm struggling to find a new accommodation so can I register again for dormitory and will I still have the financial support?  
### Answer: 

Based on the provided context, it seems that normally a student cannot stay on campus and in residence during a period of absence from their studies. However, exceptions may be considered on a case-by-case basis. Since you are a third-year student and have already moved out of the university dormitory after your first year, you would typically not be eligible to re-register for dormitory housing.

However, given your situation where you're struggling to find new accommodation, you might want to discuss your circumstances with the Student Financial Services team. They could potentially provide assistance or alternative solutions, such as temporary housing options or extensions, to help you manage your financial support while finding a new place to live.

It's important to note that you should also consider reaching out to the Residential Life staff to understand the specific policies and procedures regarding re-registration for dormitory housing and the potential impact on your financial aid. They can provide more detailed guidance based on your individual situation. 

In summary, while you may not automatically be eligible to re-register for dormitory housing, discussing your situation with the Student Financial Services and Residential Life teams could lead to a solution that supports both your academic progress and your financial needs.

### Question 93: Can you give me the procedure to request for funds to support club activities?  
### Answer: 

To request for funds to support club activities, you should follow these steps:

1. Determine the specific needs and resources required for your club's activities based on the detailed design, such as equipment, glassware, chemicals, etc.

2. Perform a thorough literature review on your topic, paying special attention to the methods employed in previous studies and their pros and cons. This will help you understand what resources are commonly used and how they have been applied successfully in similar situations.

3. Consult with your advisors, IS faculty, and lab technicians to refine your list of required resources. This will help ensure that you have considered all necessary factors and that your requests are reasonable and achievable.

4. Secure the required resources as soon as possible. For physical samples, consider your access to the places and materials. For equipment and chemicals, check with the lab technician about their availability. If they are not available, explore alternative options such as finding other institutions where FUV students can access the equipment, applying for funding from FUV or other sources, or discussing potential changes to the experimental design with your advisors.

5. Be aware that obtaining all these resources, including funding, equipment, samples, etc., may require significant paperwork. Examples include applications for funding, disbursements of funds, lead times on purchases, and getting approval from external institutions for access to samples and/or equipment.

6. Complete the process as soon as possible to ensure that you have the necessary resources for your club activities. By following these steps, you can increase your chances of securing the funds and resources needed to support your club's activities effectively.

### Question 94: How many ways are there provided by the university can I get the support in my academic path?  
### Answer: 

There are two ways provided by the university to get support in your academic path. The first one is mentorship and industry involvement, which includes having industry mentors for project guidance and potentially joining the capstone panel. The second way is through access to labs, tools, and software relevant to your project work, along with support for learning new software or techniques where necessary.

### Question 97: I'm having some bad experience with a professor teaching a course. The problem was his way of delivering does not meet academic standard and I want to say something about this with people having higher authorities. What should I do?  
### Answer: 

According to the provided context, if you believe there has been an error in grading, bias, or failure to follow published grading policies, you should first discuss the matter with the course instructor(s). If the issue remains unresolved, you may file an appeal by submitting the Review of Final Grade Request form to the Registrar's Office within five business days from the date on which the Registrar's Office posts the final grade for the term. The Registrar's Office will inform the Dean’s Office of the case. After investigation, if the Deans can mediate, no further action is required. Otherwise, the Registrar's Office will organize a panel review with the Dean’s Office for an independent evaluation of the grade. The grade determined after this evaluation shall be the final grade. Therefore, you should start by discussing the issue with the professor and then follow the appeals process outlined above. However, it's important to note that the appeals process is specifically for disputing grades, not for addressing concerns about the professor's teaching methods or delivery style. For those issues, you might consider speaking with the department chair or other relevant administrative personnel.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
APPEALS: A student who wishes to dispute a final grade in a course should first discuss the matter with the course instructor(s). If the matter remains unresolved and the student believes there has been an error in grading, bias, or failure to follow published grading policies, the student may file an appeal as follows: • Submit the Review of Final Grade Request form to the Registrar's Office within five (05) business days from the date on which the Registrar's Office posts the final grade for the term. • The Registrar's Office informs the Dean’s Office of the case. After investigation, if the Deans can mediate, no further action is required. Otherwise, the Registrar's Office organizes a panel review with the Dean’s Office for an independent evaluation of the grade. The grade determined after this evaluation shall be the final grade. In cases concerning the interpretation of a course policy, the Dean’s Office will defer to the course syllabus whenever possible and otherwise will make a final ruling on the

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
• The Registrar's Office informs the Dean’s Office of the case. After investigation, if the Deans can mediate, no further action is required. Otherwise, the Registrar's Office organizes a panel review with the Dean’s Office for an independent evaluation of the grade. The grade determined after this evaluation shall be the final grade. In cases concerning the interpretation of a course policy, the Dean’s Office will defer to the course syllabus whenever possible and otherwise will make a final ruling on the matter.

### Question 98: I'm a third year student and don't know if I should do a capstone project then where should I go to get advice?  
### Answer: 

You should go to the IS faculty to get advice about whether you should do a capstone project or not. They can help you determine the suitability and feasibility of your proposed project and guide you through the process. Early consultation is strongly encouraged.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: History Capstone Handbook - 2025-26.pdf, Page: 9]
The Capstone project is a year-long undertaking with less structure than a traditional course. It is certainly not the easiest way to complete your degree, and it may not be the most logical option for you, depending on your interests and your post-graduation plans. You should not consider it to be the default pathway to finishing your degree. One of the best reasons to undertake a Capstone project is if you enjoy doing historical research (which you will have sampled in Hands-On History and the research seminars you have completed) and want an opportunity to carry out a long-term research project. For such students, the Capstone year provides time and guidance that is unparalleled by any course or other opportunity at the undergraduate level. However, if you wish to graduate with distinction—an honorable goal— but you don’t particularly enjoy doing independent research, you may want to skip the Capstone and focus on GPA honors instead! Normally, the Capstone sequence begins in the Fall with Capstone I and

[Source: History Capstone Handbook - 2025-26.pdf, Page: 9]
projects Group project proposals will not be considered. The Capstone is intended as an individual undertaking and will be evaluated as such. There are other opportunities for group research. 1.8. Capstone I In Capstone I, you will actively conduct research and refine your project proposal and plan. You will focus on gathering and organizing your information or other materials needed to realize your project. In some cases, students may begin the very initial stages of production (subject to your advisors’ approval). Capstone I will be assessed by a combination of your active participation in the advising processes and end-of-term submission. The end-of-term submission will demonstrate successful progress towards the final Capstone submission, and satisfactory completion. Students could find a secondary advisor at other institutions, more on this in section 1.3. At the undergraduate level, we are not expecting ground breaking work from students but the projects must be original and cannot be an exact repeat of previous works either from the student or from publised literature. This originality might take different forms such as different research subjects, different methodolgy or scopes…Students are strongly encouraged to discuss with IS faculty prior to submitting the capstone proposal. 1.3. General Information: A culmination to the student’s curriculum, the capstone is an individual project that demonstrates the principal learning outcomes and competencies of that curriculum in a meaningful and coherent way. The capstone may also draw from relevant extra-curricular activities and practical experience to support the research and realization of the project. The capstone should evidence competency in a primary disciplinary specialization (optionally supported by secondary and tertiary disciplinary areas). In the Art & Media Studies major, the capstone could take the form of a thesis, an art work, or a film. For other kinds of projects, please consult with your prospective advisor(s) early in your junior year to determine the suitability and feasibility of your proposed project. Remember, the capstone should demonstrate original critical and creative thinking, and we encourage primary research. However, it should not require extensive fieldwork. ### Question 99: I'm a member of Fulbright Basketball Club and going to attend a tournament. I need the official transcript and asking for some absence in classes then where should I get help?  
### Answer: 

You should contact the faculty or supervising staff associated with the Fulbright Basketball Club to request an Official Activity Excused Absence Request Form. They will need to fill out the form and submit it to the Dean’s Office, keeping Academic Affairs and Registrar’s Office informed for the record. Ensure you provide proof of your attendance at the tournament, such as an invitation letter or acceptance email, along with proof of your travel. After the event, submit a 300-500 word reflection paper to ug.academic.affairs@fulbright.edu.vn within 7 days of your return. Remember to discuss any absence with your instructors and make arrangements to make up any missed work. Fulbright's Academic Affairs team or Registrar’s Office can also be contacted during business hours if you face any emergencies preventing you from following these instructions. Lastly, ensure you inform the Office of the Registrar upon your return and register for classes using the One-Stop platform for the term you're returning to.

### Question 102: How to work with major report?  
### Answer: 

To work effectively on the major report, start by understanding the specific requirements and expectations outlined for the report. This includes knowing the structure, content, and any formatting guidelines that need to be followed. Begin early to ensure ample time for research, writing, and revision. Engage regularly with your academic advisors to get feedback and guidance throughout the process. Make sure to meet all deadlines for submissions, such as uploading presentation slides and demonstration videos by the specified date. Additionally, prepare thoroughly for the Q&A session with the judging panel and audience, ensuring you are well-informed about your project's details, simulation/prototype, testing/experimental results, and future work recommendations. Finally, review and finalize your report according to the provided criteria, ensuring it meets all necessary standards before submission. This approach will help you produce a comprehensive and high-quality major report.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: HCE_Capstone_Handbook_Final_2025.01.16.pdf, Page: 5]
followed by up to 10 minutes for Q&A with the judging panel and audience. • Submission Requirements: ▪ Final report: Submit your individual report on Canvas and provide a copy to the judging panel members at least 7 days before the last day of the semester. The report should include: ➢ Final design: Detailed description of the system or product. ➢ Simulation/Prototype details: Explain the setup and functionality. ➢ Testing/Experimental results: Provide data and analysis of the outcomes. ➢ Conclusion: Summarize what has been achieved and the impact of your work. ➢ Future work: Offer recommendations for further development or research. ▪ Additional deliverables ➢ By 5:00pm on the last day of the semester, upload your presentation slides and any demonstration videos onto Canvas.

Evaluation Reports The primary written deliverable for the Capstone by Applied and Creative Project is the Evaluation Report. The Evaluation Report includes • (1) the intellectual rationale of the project and its expected contributions to a given academic field within social studies, • * (2) the goals of the project, • (3) the evaluation questions regarding the degree to which the project met its goals, and • (4) a critical evaluation that answers the evaluation questions based on the documentation of the process (see below) and any data collected. Scoring of the evaluation report is based on the completeness, critical depth, intellectual rigor, and effective use of evidence and theory, not on whether the project appears to have met its goals. The appendix of the Evaluation Report includes documentation of the process, consisting of relevant research, material experimentation, timelines, documentary photographs of the

### Question 103: How many way can I fill in the requirements of EL?  
### Answer: 

You can fulfill the requirements of the Fulbright's Experiential Learning Program (ELP) in up to 12 credits, with a minimum of 4 credits being mandatory for graduation. This can be done through various streams managed by Academic Affairs (AA), Career Services (CS), and Center for Entrepreneurship and Innovation (CEI). Additionally, experiential learning can also count towards elective or major requirements with advisor approval. Therefore, there are multiple ways to meet the ELP requirements depending on your course selection and advisor approval.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: CS_Capstone_Guideline_v2_Dec_20_2024.pdf, Page: 2]
2. Eligibility criteria ..................................................................................................................... 1:

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
count toward elective or major requirements (upon advisor approval). Fulbright’s Experiential Learning Program (ELP) exists to create, standardize, and facilitate academic credit-bearing experiential learning experiences. All full-time, undergraduate, degree- seeking students must complete at least 04 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the ELP as a graduation requirement. Current ELP streams are housed within Academic Affairs (AA), Career Services (CS), and Center for Entrepreneurship and Innovation (CEI), where each team is responsible for administrative and academic duties of their respective stream(s). The ELP operates within Fulbright’s undergraduate program’s standard operating procedures and is developed in consultation with undergraduate program leadership and faculty. For more details, please refer here https://onestop.fulbright.edu.vn/s/article/Experiential-Learning- Program 13.5  Electives To complete the degree, students are free to take elective courses from the Course Catalogue.
